тАШ рдЖ рд╡реЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореН ред рдЖ рд╡рдГ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧ рдЙрдХреНрддрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

3 (299)
Agni
V─Бmadeva Gautama
16 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
In the very last verse of this hymn (16) the poet announces that he has produced counsels, enigmas, secret words, and poetry for Agni: these verbal products presum ably make up the rest of the hymn. It begins fairly straightforwardly, however, with a treatment (vss. 1тАУ3) of the kindling of the ritual fire, as so often at the beginning of Agni hymns. But starting with verse 4 a certain worried tone becomes apparent, about the relationship between the poet and the god Agni. The next four verses (5тАУ8) contain anxious questions: what is Agni planning to say to various gods about us? These questions reflect the uncertainty produced by the ritual model: Agni is the ritual mediator between men and gods, and so in some sense everything the gods learn about us mortals is filtered through Agni, who may beтАФwe worryтАФan unreli
able witness. The anxiety returns in verses 13тАУ14, especially the former, in which the poet worries that Agni will punish him for the deeds of his relatives and acquain tances. In between (vss. 9тАУ12) are four verses, each beginning with the charged word r╠еt├йna тАЬby truth,тАЭ introducing a mixture of ritual and mythic activities, including
one verse (11) on the Vala myth, a preoccupation of the Agni hymns in IV. What ties the various parts of the hymn together is not entirely clear, and it may be that the poetтАЩs final verse, listing several types of verbal material, is meant to indicate that the hymn consists of a disparate collection of his works, although attempting to assign those labels to the different parts of the hymn would probably be taking the conceit too far.

Jamison Brereton Notes

English translation:

тАЬSecure Agni, the king of sacrifice, the afflicter (of foes), the invoker (of the gods), the distributor of food through heaven and earth, the golden-formed, for your protection before (surprised by) sudden death.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pur─Б tanayitnor acitt─Бt = liс╣н, before the unconsciousness of the thunderbolt; this implies a state of unconsciousness, or death as sudden as if the work of the thunderbolt

Jamison Brereton

Make [=ignite] him here, the king, the Rudra of your ceremony, the Hotar whose sacrifice comes true in the two world-halves,
Agni of golden formтАФ(make him) for help for you in the face of
unexpected thundering.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I render vs.-final kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam twice – once with vs.-initial ─Б╠Бin the meaning тАШmake = kindleтАЩ, rather than with most tr. тАШbring hereтАЩ, and once with the quasiinfinitival dat. ├бvase.

It is not entirely clear why Agni is identified as Rudra here. The word is most likely to be construed with the gen. adhvar├бsya as тАЬthe Rudra of the/your ceremony,тАЭ on the basis of I.114.4 rudr├бс╣Г yaj├▒as─Б╠Бdham тАЬRudra bringing the sacrifice to successтАЭ and III.2.5 (also of Agni) rudr├бс╣Г yaj├▒─Б╠Бn─Бс╣Г s─Б╠Бdhadiс╣гс╣нim тАЬthe Rudra of the sacrifices, bringing success to the offerings.тАЭ Perhaps the point of comparison is RudraтАЩs healing powers and, esp. here, his ability to ward off threats of all sorts, in this case the тАЬunexpected thunderingтАЭ (tanayitn├│r ac├нtt─Бt) of p─Бda c.

r├│dasyoс╕е can be either gen. (with most tr.) or loc. (so published translation). There is little riding on the choice.

As most interpr. take it, тАЬunexpected thunderingтАЭ is probably a reference to all sorts of unforeseen dangers, rather than specifically of a sudden storm.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЖрдкреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╡реЛрд╜рдзреНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реЗ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕рддреНрдпрдпрдЬрдВ рд░реБрджреНрд░рдордЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╛рддреН рддрдирдпрд┐рддреНрдиреЛрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрд░реВрдкрдВ рд░реЛрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрд░рдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдВ рдкреБрд░рд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдо рддрдерд╛рднреВрддрдорд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдиреГрдкрдВ рдпреВрдпрдорд╛рдХреГрдгреБрдзреНрд╡рдореН реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрди рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирдХреГрддреНрдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдп) рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рд░реБрджреНрд░рдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд░реЛрджрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН (рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдореН) рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН (рд╕рддреНрдпрдпрдЬрдореН) рдпрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрдореЗрд╡ рдпрдЬрддрд┐ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреЗ рддрдореН (рд░реЛрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрдГ) рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрд░реНрдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдорд┐рд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдкреБрд░рд╛) рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН (рддрдирдпрд┐рддреНрдиреЛрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдГ (рдЕрдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╛рддреН) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрдВ рдпрддреНрд░ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН (рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрд░реВрдкрдореН) рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рддреЗрдЬрд╕реЛ рд░реВрдкрдорд┐рд╡ рд░реВрдкрдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрдореН (рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ) рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдордирд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдирд╛рдп (рдХреГрдгреБрдзреНрд╡рдореН) реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреИрд░реЗрдХрд╕рдореНрдорддрд┐рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдпрдереЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЗрдг рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдбрд╕реНрдп рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рд╕рд╛рдзрд┐рддрдВ рддрдерд╛рднреВрддрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдорд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╜рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрдВ рдиреГрдкрдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕рд╛рдзрдпрдд рдпрддреЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдордкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рд╕рд┐рдзреНрдпреЗрддреН реерезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis is the altar which we have decorated for you, as a wife attached to her husband puts on elegant garments (to gratify him); maturer of good works, sit down in our presence invested (with radiance), while your flames incline towards you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here is the womb that we made for you. (It is/You are) like an eager wife, richly dressed, for her husband.
Enveloped, sit down facing our way: here are (hymns) facing you, o very knowing one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All the standard tr. take the rel. cl. of p─Бda a (cakс╣Ыm─Б╠Бy├бс╣Г vay├бm te тАЬ[the womb] which we have made for youтАЭ) as the frame for the simile in b, with тАЬweтАЭ matching the eager wife (j─Б╠Бy─Б тАж u┼Ыat─л╠Б) and тАЬyouтАЭ (Agni) matching the husband. Oldenberg (SBE) goes so far as to supply тАЬmarriage-bedтАЭ as the match for the womb: тАЬтАж as a well-dressed loving wife (prepares the marriage-bed) for her husband.тАЭ This is one possible reading, but I donтАЩt think it is the only (or even the dominant) one; in fact, I think the simile can be matched to four different entities in the verse.

Let us begin by noting that p─Бda b, the self-contained simile, is found three times elsewhere (I.124.7 of Dawn, X.71.4 of V─Бc, and X.91.13 of praise [suс╣гс╣нut├н-] seeking Agni), in all cases of females or of entities conceived as female. An obvious тАЬentity conceived as femaleтАЭ is found in the nominal main clause of p─Бda a, ay├бс╣Г y├│niс╕е тАЬhere is the wombтАЭ: the womb, though grammatically masc., is a female accoutrement and can be matched with the wife in the simile in b. This тАЬwombтАЭ (=fireplace) is well prepared (тАЬrichly dressedтАЭ suv─Б╠Бs─Бс╕е) and ready to receive Agni as her husband. For womb = wife, cf. III.53.4 j─Бy├йd тАж s├йd u y├│niс╕е тАЬThe wife – just she is the womb.тАЭ But suv─Б╠Бs─Бс╕е elsewhere occurs in the same p─Бda with p├бriv─лtaс╕е (found in our p─Бda c): III.8.4a y├║v─Б suv─Б╠Б s─Бс╕е p├бriv─лta ─Б╠Б g─Бt тАЬAs a youth, richly dressed, engirded, he has come here.тАЭ Although the referent there is the sacrifical post, the vocabulary is also appropriate to Agni. Therefore it could be the Agni of c who is like a wife, eager for her husband identified with the womb in p─Бda a – a gender reversal that would appeal to the Rigvedic poets. (Note that the standard reading, where тАЬweтАЭ the ritualists match the wife, also requires some gender reversal.) Finally let us consider p─Бda d. The subj. of d is fem., expressed by im─Б╠Бu te тАж prat─лc─л╠Бh тАЬthese facing you.тАЭ Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) supply тАЬFrauen,тАЭ but in n. 2d Geldner suggests g├нraс╕е (inter alia); Renou supplies тАЬlouanges.тАЭ I think g├нraс╕е must be correct: there are a number of im─Б╠Бu tv─Б/te тАж g├нraс╕е passages (e.g. VI.45.25, 28, VII.18.3, VIII.3.3), and Geldner/Renou adduce V.12.1 for gir- as well: g├нram bhare vr╠ес╣гabh─Б╠Б ya prat─лc─л ╠Б m. As was noted above, in 2 of its 4 occurrences the тАЬeager wifeтАЭ simile has speech/praise as its comparandum, so in fact that simile in our b works best with the hymns in d: these hymns face towards you, like an eager wife to(wards) her husband.

Bloomfield discusses the simile at length ad I.124.7. He is rather sour about our passage: the construction is тАЬvery loose indeedтАЭ; тАЬthe metaphor limps decidedly.тАЭ Contra Bloomfield I consider the deployment of the simile here as an example of the poetтАЩs extreme cleverness, with the simile applicable to every single entity in the vs. To reflect the polyvalent status of the simile, the published translation should probably be changed to тАЬ(It is / we are / you are / they are) like тАж,тАЭ though this would be very clumsy.

As for p├бriv─лta- тАШenvelopedтАЩ in c, the question is what Agni is enveloped in. It could be the paridhi sticks that surround the ritual fire (see, e.g., Geldner ad I.128.1, endorsed for that passage by Thieme [Unters. 19]); Witzel Got┼Н suggest dawnтАЩs light or hymns; Oldenberg (SBE) offerings and prayers. ItтАЩs useful to note that p├бriv─лta- occurs twice with the loc. of y├│ni-: once in an Agni hymn X.46.6 p├бriv─лto y├│nau s─лdad ant├бс╕е (note тИЪsad here as well) and once in the riddle hymn I.164.32 s├б m─Бt├║r y├│n─Б p├бriv─лto ant├бс╕е, so that the two concepts seem to be connected (тАЬenveloped within the wombтАЭ).

This could fit the paridhi sticks forming a border of the fireplace conceived as a womb. It might also refer to the kindling sticks, within which fire is hidden until he is ignited (/born), hence also his womb. There is another important parallel in nearby 1.7 anant├й ant├бс╕е p├бriv─лta ─Б╠Бg─Бt тАЬenveloped within the limitless, he has come hereтАЭ; see comm. there. On the multiple meanings of p├бriv─лta- in Agni context, see Thieme (Unters., 19-20).

Modern tr. (almost) universally take the voc. svap─Бka- as тАШhaving a lovely backsideтАЩ vel sim., related to ├бp─Б├▒c- тАШturned backwardsтАЩ and here implicitly contrasting with prat─лc─л╠Бс╕е тАШturned towards, facingтАЩ. The one exception is Oldenberg, who in SBE (1897) tr. тАЬO most skilful one,тАЭ an interpr. that he swiftly disavowed (ZDMG 55 [1901]: 301 [=KlSch. 760]) as тАЬnicht zu denkenтАЭ – without admitting he had in fact thought it previously. Nonetheless, I think this is a more appealing interpr. than the current standard. I take it as built to a negated ├б-p─Бka- тАШnot na├пve, not callowтАЩ to p─Б╠Бka- тАШna├пve, callow, simpleтАЩ – like ├бm┼лra- тАШnot stupidтАЩ: m┼лr├б- тАШstupidтАЩ. ├бm┼лra- is found three times in the Agni hymns of this maс╣Зс╕Нala (IV.4.12, 6.2, 11.5), always of Agni. The semantically similar ├бdс╣Ыpita- тАШundistractedтАЩ in the next p─Бda (3a) supports this interpr. There are two other occurrences of sv├бp─Бka- (VI.11.4, 12.2), both analyzed by the Pp as s├║ ├бp─Бka- (both adduced by Oldenberg, SBE), both modifying Agni.

In neither case does a тАЬhaving a lovely backsideтАЭ impose (or even suggest) itself, and I propose to include them under this stem.

Griffith

This shrine have we made ready for thy coming, as the fond dame attires her for her husband.
Performer of good work, sit down before us, invested while these flames incline to meet thee.

Oldenberg

This is the home which we have prepared for thee as a well-dressed, loving wife (prepares the marriage-bed) for her husband 1. Directed hitherward, dressed (in offerings and prayers?) 2 sit down. These (sacrificial ladles or prayers?) are turned towards thee, O most skilful one 3!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRepeat, oс╕е priest, the praise, the prayer, to the attentive, the affable Agni, the beholder of man, the giver of felicity, the divine, the immortal; to him whom the effuser of the libation, like the (bruising) stone, adores aloud.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To him [=Agni] who listens undistracted to the thought, to the one drawing the gaze of men, the very gracious oneтАФo ritual adeptтАФ
to the god, the immortal, chant the chant, the god whom the (human) presser invokes like the honey-pressing pressing stone.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes the voc. vedhaс╕е as the poetтАЩs self-address, which is certainly possible; he is commanding himself to recite (┼Ыaс╣Гsa). This does not solve the question of the person of the verb ─лс╕╖├й in d. Although this form is universally rendered (incl. in the published tr) as a 3rd sg. (and analyzed, because of its accent, as the only perfect form to this root, against root pres. ─л╠Бс╕╖e, ─л╠Бс╣нс╣нe; see K├╝mmel 122), it could of course also be a 1st sg. pf., with s├│t─Б an appositive to the underlying 1st ps. subj. (тАЬI the presserтАЭ). Since the surrounding vss. (2 and 4) have explicit 1st persons (though pl.), I would be inclined to emend the published translation to тАЬwhom I, the presser, invoke тАжтАЭ P─Бda d plays on the standard Rigvedic notion that the soma-pressing stones are very noisy and that their noise is like that of the priestly recitation and singing happening at the same time. The question here is which of the three terms in the phrase gr─Б╠Бveva s├│t─Б madhuс╣г├║t belongs to the simile and which to the frame. On the basis of X.64.15 gr─Б╠Бvev─Б y├бtra madhuс╣г├║d ucy├бte bс╣Ыh├бt, I take gr─Б╠Бv─Б тАж madhuс╣г├║t тАЬthe honey-pressing (pressing) stoneтАЭ as a discontinuous simile, with the frame represented by s├│t─Б in between. Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н, K├╝mmel (122), and Scarlatta (615) take the simile to be gr─Б╠Бveva s├│t─Б and the frame madhuс╣г├║t; Oldenberg (SBE) confines the simile to gr─Б╠Бv─Б with the frame s├│t─Б madhuс╣г├║t. Either of these configurations avoids a discontinuous simile, but such similes are not rare and the phraseology of X.64.15 supports my analysis. Little rests on it, however.

Griffith

A hymn, O Priest, to him who hears, the gentle, to him who looks on men, exceeding gracious,
A song of praise sing to the God Immortal, whom the stone, presser of the sweet juice, worships.

Oldenberg

To him who hears us, who is not proud, who beholds men, to the merciful, immortal god recite a prayer, O worshipper, a hymnтАФ(to Agni) whom the presser (of Soma), the Madhu-presser, magnifies like the pressing-stone 1.

Geldner

Ihm, der nicht zerstreut zuh├╢rt, trag, o Meister, das Gedicht vor, dem gn├дdigen mit dem Herrenauge, dem unsterblichen Gotte das Preislied, den der Honigpresser ruft wie der pressende Stein.

Grassmann

Dem holdgesinnten, welcher h├╢rt und aufmerkt, dem m├дnnerschaunden sprich Gebet, Verehrer; Dem Gotte, dem Unsterblichen ein Loblied, ihn ruf’ ich, wie der Stein, der Soma keltert.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou Agni, preside over this our rite; do you who are cognizant of truth, and the author of good works, recognize this our adoration, whenever these exhilarating prayers (are addressed) to you whenever friendly relations with you are (established) in our dwelling.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni, at least become aware of this (ritual) labor of ours, of (our expression of) truth, o perceiver of truth, as one who is very
concerned.
When will our solemn words become your feasting companions? When will your fellowship (come to) be in our house?

Jamison Brereton Notes

My тАЬat leastтАЭ for cid follows Geldner (тАЬwenigstensтАЭ). This somewhat testy note seems to introduce the next part of the hymn, with its anxious or annoyed questions to Agni about his relationship to the sacrificers and how he will represent it to the other gods.

The ┼Ы├бm─л- and the с╣Ыt├б- here presumably refer to the complementary physical and verbal aspects of the sacrifice. On с╣Ыt├б- as тАЬKultliedтАЭ in this and similar passages, see L├╝ders (esp. 442-43).

Griffith

Even as true knower of the Law, O Agni, to this our solemn rite he thou attentive.
When shall thy songs of festival be sung thee? When is thy friendship shown within our dwelling?

Oldenberg

Thou who art well-intentioned, give heed to this our toiling 1, to this Rita 2, O observer of Rita! When will our hymns share in thy rejoicings? When will our friendship dwell in thy house?

Geldner

Merke du wenigstens auf diesen Opferdienst von uns, o Agni, wohlmeinend auf das rechte Werk, des Rechten Kundiger! Wann werden dir die Loblieder zum Mittrunk recht sein? Wann wird deine Freundschaft im Hause sein?

Grassmann

Beachte recht dies unser Werk, o Agni, den frommen Brauch, o Kenner frommen Brauches; Wann t├╢nen dir die frohen Festges├дnge? wann schliesst sich Freundschaft dir in deinem Hause?

Elizarenkova

тАЬWhy, Agni, do you reproach us (for our sin) to Varuс╣Зa, why to the heaven? what is our offence? why repeat it to the bountiful Mitra, to earth, to Aryaman, or to Bhaga?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How will you complain about this to Varuс╣Зa, o Agni, how to Heaven? What is our offense?

Aryaman, to Fortune?

The last p─Бda would be more accurately rendered тАЬWhat to Aryaman, what to Fortune?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The list of gods to whom Agni will tattle on us follows a certain pattern.

Vs. 5 contains the standard great trio of ─Аdityas, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, and Aryaman, as well as a minor ─Аditya, Bhaga тАШFortuneтАЩ, who is, however, important for our welfare.

Although we might have expected the Sun here, because he serves as the ─АdityasтАЩ eye, observing our offenses, we have instead Heaven and Earth, which frame the cosmos. In vs. 6 the nearer gods of the midspace, particularly V─Бta тАШwindтАЩ and the A┼Ыvins, are featured. Rudra appears in both 6 and 7; I donтАЩt quite understand why, but recall first that Agni was identified as Rudra in vs. 1 and may be also in 10d (see also 14b). Moreover, in 6 the punishing aspect of Rudra is emphasized (тАШmansmitingтАЩ, nс╣Ыh├бn-), while in 7 he is paired and/or contrasted with the benevolent P┼лс╣гan under the ambiguous epithet s├║makha-, which means both тАШgood combatantтАЩ and тАШvery generousтАЩ, so his effects on human life are emphasized and he counts as a nearer god, who in fact is the giver of the oblation (havird─Б╠Б-). In the 2nd half of 7 Viс╣гс╣Зu and his three strides return us to the contemplation of the whole cosmos, and vs. 8 functions ring-compositionally with vs. 5: we have the Sun we expected (and didnтАЩt get) in 5, with Aditi standing in for the ─Аdityas in 5, and heaven (though probably the place, not the deity) is the final goal.

Griffith

Why this complaint to Varuna, O Agni? And why to Heaven? for what is our transgression?
How wilt thou speak to Earth and bounteous Mitra? What wilt thou say to Aryaman and Bhaga?

Oldenberg

How wilt thou, O Agni, before Varuna, and how wilt thou, and which sin of ours wilt thou blame before Dyaus? How wilt thou speak to bountiful Mitra, to the Earth? What (wilt thou say) to Aryaman, to Bhaga?

English translation:

тАЬWhy repeat it when exalted in holy ceremonies? why tell it to the mighty, benevolent, circumambient, truthful wind? why, Agni, to earth, why to man-destroying Rudra?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

What (will you say), Agni, having grown strong on the holy places [=ritual hearths], what to the Wind projecting strength, charging to beauty,
(what) to the earth-circling (chariot) of the N─Бsatyas, for it to appear? What will you say, Agni, to man-smiting Rudra?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note that all four p─Бdas rhyme: agne# (a), ┼Ыubhaс╣Гy├й# (b), kс╣г├й# (c), nс╣Ыghn├й (d); also 7ab p┼лс╣гс╣З├й# тАж havird├й#, an unusual effect in RVic verse.

The so-called тАЬdouble stemтАЭ vс╣Ыdhas─Бn├б- is morphologically anomalous, but belongs to a fairly large group of stems with apparent middle part. in -as─Бn├б-. This is not the place to treat the origin of these stems at length, but, with Insler (KZ 82 [1968]), I think the starting point is sahas─Бn├б- (5x, 4x of Agni) тАШdisplaying mightтАЩ, which he takes as a metathesized form of a pf. mid. part. *sasah─Бn├б-, beside s─Бsah─Бn├б- (1x) and the younger type seh─Бn├б- (3x). This metathesis was reinforced by the very common s-stem s├бhas-, and several other -as─Бn├б-stems have s-stems alongside (┼Ыavas─Бn├б-: ┼Ы├бvas-, rabhas─Бn├б-: r├бbhas-, jrayas─Бn├б-: jr├бyas-) and fall into the same general semantic field of strength, power, or violent action (though not one of the best attested, mandas─Бn├б- тАШbecoming exhilaratedтАЩ nor, e.g., dhiyas─Бn├б- [2x]).

There is unfortunately no neut. s-stem *vс╣Ы╠Бdhas-, though there is a single attestation of an infinitival dat. vс╣Ыdh├бse with suffixal accent. See also disc. of vс╣Ыdhasn├║- ad IV.2.3.

P─Бda c is problematic, both metrically (it lacks a syllable) and grammatically: this is the only place in the RV where n─Б╠Бsatya- appears in the sg., not the du., and the identity of p─Бda-final kс╣г├й is disputed. The metrical problem and the kс╣г├й problem can be easily solved together if we adopt the suggestion of Hoffmann registered in Schindler (Root nouns, s.v. kс╣г─Б╠Б-) that kс╣г├й is a haplologized form of datival inf. *yakс╣г├й тАШto appearтАЩ in the environment (n─Б╠Бsati )y─Бya [ya]kс╣г├й. (Note that yakс╣г├бm тАШapparitionтАЩ appears in 13a.) This interpr. is also reflected in Witzel Got┼НтАЩs rendering, and one way or other it goes back to Ludwig; see Oldenberg (SBE, Noten). The published translation should have an asterisk before тАЬto appear.тАЭ As for sg. n─Б╠Бsaty─Бya, although this analysis is emphatically rejected by both Oldenberg (Noten) and Debrunner (AiG II.2.136), I have adopted HenryтАЩs old suggestion that the form is a vс╣Ыddhi adj. of appurtanance whose vс╣Ыddhi is invisible because the base already has initial-syllable vс╣Ыddhi. We would of course expect the accent to shift to the final syllable (AiG II.2.133ff.), hence *n─Бsaty├б-, but the dominance of the initially accented noun could have altered the accent, possibly redactionally. I supply тАШchariotтАЩ in this dat. expression, since the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot is esp. prominent and p├бrijman- modifies their chariot elsewhere (I.20.3, X.41.1). Cf. esp. I.20.3 t├бkс╣гan n─Б╠Бsaty─Бbhy─Бm p├бrijmanaс╣Г sukh├бс╣Г r├бtham тАЬThey fashioned the earth-circling wellnaved chariot for the N─Бsatyas.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The list of gods to whom Agni will tattle on us follows a certain pattern.

Vs. 5 contains the standard great trio of ─Аdityas, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, and Aryaman, as well as a minor ─Аditya, Bhaga тАШFortuneтАЩ, who is, however, important for our welfare.

Although we might have expected the Sun here, because he serves as the ─АdityasтАЩ eye, observing our offenses, we have instead Heaven and Earth, which frame the cosmos. In vs. 6 the nearer gods of the midspace, particularly V─Бta тАШwindтАЩ and the A┼Ыvins, are featured. Rudra appears in both 6 and 7; I donтАЩt quite understand why, but recall first that Agni was identified as Rudra in vs. 1 and may be also in 10d (see also 14b). Moreover, in 6 the punishing aspect of Rudra is emphasized (тАШmansmitingтАЩ, nс╣Ыh├бn-), while in 7 he is paired and/or contrasted with the benevolent P┼лс╣гan under the ambiguous epithet s├║makha-, which means both тАШgood combatantтАЩ and тАШvery generousтАЩ, so his effects on human life are emphasized and he counts as a nearer god, who in fact is the giver of the oblation (havird─Б╠Б-). In the 2nd half of 7 Viс╣гс╣Зu and his three strides return us to the contemplation of the whole cosmos, and vs. 8 functions ring-compositionally with vs. 5: we have the Sun we expected (and didnтАЩt get) in 5, with Aditi standing in for the ─Аdityas in 5, and heaven (though probably the place, not the deity) is the final goal.

English translation:

тАЬWhy to the great and nutriment-conveying P┼лс╣гan? why to Rudra, the object of worship, the giver of the oblation (to the gods)? why to the many-hymned Viс╣гс╣Зu? why tell our sin to the extensive year?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To the extensive year: ┼Ыarave bс╣Ыhatyai: ┼Ыaruс╕е, ┼Ыarat, saс╣Гvatsaraс╕е; or, ┼Ыaru = nirс╣Ыti, the feminine le person nification of evil; niс╣Ыс╣Ыti also occurs as a masculine (nirс╣Ыtir yaj├▒avigh─Бti r─Бkс╣гasaс╕е, an evil spirit disturbing sacrifice : Taittir─лya Yajus. 1.2,11);

Nirс╣Ыti = nairс╣Ыta; nirс╣Ыtir sva nairс╣Ыta iti v─Б (Amarako┼Ыa 1.1,56); narс╣Ыtos tu khasaputro rakс╣гaso nirс╣Ыtis ca saс╕е, Nairс╣Ыta, the son of Khasa, a r─Бkс╣гasa, he is also Nirс╣Ыti (Ratnako┼Ыa)

Jamison Brereton

How (will you speak) to great P┼лс╣гan who brings prosperity, what to Rudra, the good combatant [/very generous], for him to give the oblation,
what to wide-striding Viс╣гс╣Зu, (for him to give) semen? What will you say, Agni, to (RudraтАЩs) lofty arrow?

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the benevolent Rudra see comm. ad vss. 5-8. It is not clear why or how Rudra is the giver of the oblation. Oldenberg (see also Witzel Got┼НтАЩs n.) suggests that it is in his capacity as pa┼Ыupati-: he provides the beast for sacrifice. This is possible: though he is not so called in the RV (where the word is not found), this epithet is applied to him in AV (e.g., XI.2.28) and VS (e.g., XXVI.28).

In c r├йtaс╕е тАШsemenтАЩ is somewhat surprising, esp. if it is to be construed as the object of br├бvaс╕е – so much so that Grassmann (tr., not W├╢.) suggested emendation to r├йpaс╕е тАШstainтАЩ, an emendation accepted by Oldenberg (SBE, Noten) and L├╝ders (622) and maintained tentatively by Scarlatta (214). Renou keeps the transmitted form but interprets it as a way of referring to negative speech: тАЬQuelle semence (de bl├вme dirais-tu) тАж?тАЭ But in a culture so fixated on fertility, semen is basically always a positive concept. Important is the fact noted by Geldner (n. 7c) that Viс╣гс╣Зu is elsewhere the protector of semen (cf., e.g., VII.36.9 v├нс╣гс╣Зuс╣Г niс╣гiktap─Б╠Бm тАЬViс╣гс╣Зu, protector of the poured-out [semen]тАЭ). In his n.

(and contra his tr.) Renou suggests an alternative interpr. of r├йtaс╕е here as a truncated

*retodhe (cf. retodh─Б╠Б- 5x) or *retode (Renou does not accent either proposed form). This seems the correct solution, with the -de extracted from havird├й, which ended the preceding p─Бda.

In d Renou suggests that ┼Ы├бrave bс╣Ыhatya├н is the тАЬ├йtat pr├й-compositionnelтАЭ of a bahuvr─лhi *bс╣Ыhat┼Ыarave (no accent provided and no application of sandhi), whose referent is Rudra. Although the arrow is surely RudraтАЩs as all standard interpr.

recognize, there is no reason to substitute the god for his symbolic accoutrement. Just as Agni can speak to the chariot of the A┼Ыvins (6c, by my interpr.), he can also speak to RudraтАЩs arrow.

Geldner (n. 7d) points out the contrast between Viс╣гс╣Зu as creator (c) and Rudra as destroyer (d).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The list of gods to whom Agni will tattle on us follows a certain pattern.

Vs. 5 contains the standard great trio of ─Аdityas, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, and Aryaman, as well as a minor ─Аditya, Bhaga тАШFortuneтАЩ, who is, however, important for our welfare.

Although we might have expected the Sun here, because he serves as the ─АdityasтАЩ eye, observing our offenses, we have instead Heaven and Earth, which frame the cosmos. In vs. 6 the nearer gods of the midspace, particularly V─Бta тАШwindтАЩ and the A┼Ыvins, are featured. Rudra appears in both 6 and 7; I donтАЩt quite understand why, but recall first that Agni was identified as Rudra in vs. 1 and may be also in 10d (see also 14b). Moreover, in 6 the punishing aspect of Rudra is emphasized (тАШmansmitingтАЩ, nс╣Ыh├бn-), while in 7 he is paired and/or contrasted with the benevolent P┼лс╣гan under the ambiguous epithet s├║makha-, which means both тАШgood combatantтАЩ and тАШvery generousтАЩ, so his effects on human life are emphasized and he counts as a nearer god, who in fact is the giver of the oblation (havird─Б╠Б-). In the 2nd half of 7 Viс╣гс╣Зu and his three strides return us to the contemplation of the whole cosmos, and vs. 8 functions ring-compositionally with vs. 5: we have the Sun we expected (and didnтАЩt get) in 5, with Aditi standing in for the ─Аdityas in 5, and heaven (though probably the place, not the deity) is the final goal.

Griffith

How to great Pusan who promotes our welfare,- to honoured Rudra what, who gives oblations?
What sin of ours to the far-striding Visnu, what, Agni, wilt thou tell the Lofty Arrow.

Geldner

Wie wirst du zum gro├Яen Pusan sprechen, dem Nahrungsbringer? Was zu Rudra, dem Freigebigen, der die Opfer austeilt? Welchen Samen wirst du dem weitschreitenden Visnu empfehlen, welchen dem hohen Gescho├Я ├╝berantworten, o Agni?

Grassmann

Was willst dem grossen Nahrungbringer Puschan, dem kampfge├╝bten Somatrinker Rudra, Dem Weithinschreiter Vischnu welches Unrecht, was, Agni, sagen du dem grossen Speergott?

English translation:

тАЬWhy tell it to the veracious company of the Maruts? why, even when asked, to the mighty sun? why repeat it to Aditi, or to the swift wind? fulfil, all-knowing J─Бtavedas, (the worship) of heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How (will you speak) to the troop of Maruts, for truth? How to the lofty Sun? When you are asked,
(how) will you answer to Aditi, to powerful (Indra?)? Send (our thought) to its goal, all the way to heavenтАФ(you are) the observant one, o J─Бtavedas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although it is tempting to take с╣Ыt─Б╠Бya as an adj. modifying ┼Ы├бrdh─Бya (so, e.g., Geldner тАЬder rechtwandelnden Schar,тАЭ sim. Witzel Got┼Н, Oldenberg SBE), the stem с╣Ыt├б- is overwhelmingly a neut. noun. It is possible, with Renou, to take it as an appositive with the Marut troop: тАЬOrdre (incarn├й)тАЭ or, with L├╝ders (623), as a separate entity to whom AgniтАЩs speech is directed, but I think it more likely that it is a dative of purpose, like (ya)kс╣г├й in 6d, havird├й in 7b: тАЬfor truth,тАЭ that is, for the Maruts to attain or ascertain the truth.

The masc. (/neut.) tur─Б╠Бya cannot modify fem. ├бditaye (pace Oldenberg SBE). Geldner supplies тАЬheavenтАЭ; Witzel Got┼Н suggest the sun. With Renou I opt tentatively for Indra, who is frequently modified by this adj. and who is otherwise absent from this fairly comprehensive list of important gods (see Geldner n. 8c). Brereton (─Аdityas, 205-6) instead thinks tur─Б╠Бya represents an ─Аditya, probably Varuс╣Зa, and takes ├бditaye not as the name of the goddess but as a common noun тАШinnocenceтАЩ, with the dative phrase meaning тАЬfor the mighty one (=Varuс╣Зa) to (ascertain our) innocence.тАЭ This assertion of innocence at the end of a series of questions about potential blame would set the stage for the request that Agni make our sacrifice succeed (p─Бda d). This suggestion is appealing, but I am not convinced that ├бditi- ever means тАШinnocenceтАЩ, and further in this sequence the purpose datives are only p─Бda-final, which ├бditaye is not.

P─Бda d poses some syntactic challenges. The first is that s─Б╠Бdh─Б, by all accounts a 2nd sg. act. impv. to тИЪs─Бdh, has no expressed obj., though act. forms of this root are fundamentally tr. (but sometimes, esp. in the participle, used in absolute sense тАЬassuring successтАЭ; cf. nearby IV.1.9). I supply dh├нyam тАШthoughtтАЩ vel sim. as the object, since forms of dh─л╠Б- or other words for thought/prayer are regularly construed with тИЪs─Бdh. The other problem is what to construe gen./abl. div├бс╕е with. (It cannot be acc. pl. because of the accent.) The standard solution has been to take it with cikitv─Б╠Бn (e.g., Geldner тАЬder du den Himmel kennstтАЭ), but as Renou points out, cikitv─Б╠Бn is never otherwise construed with a gen. His solution is to supply an obj. for s─Б╠Бdh─Б on which div├бс╕е is dependent: тАЬM├иne droit au but (les affaires) du ciel.тАЭ My interpr.

requires a slight emendation, from s─Б╠Бdh─Б div├бс╕е to *s─Б╠Бdh─Б╠Бdiv├бс╕е – that is, s─Б╠Бdha ─Б╠Б div├бс╕е, with ─Б╠Б+ ABL in the meaning тАЬall the way to.тАЭ Cf. I.92.17 ya├║ тАж ┼Ыl├│kam ─Б╠Б div├бс╕е тАж cakr├бthuс╕е тАЬyou two who made your signal-call (reach) all the way to heavenтАЭ; sim. III.61.4. See comm. ad locc. An asterisk should be inserted before тАЬall the way.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The list of gods to whom Agni will tattle on us follows a certain pattern.

Vs. 5 contains the standard great trio of ─Аdityas, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, and Aryaman, as well as a minor ─Аditya, Bhaga тАШFortuneтАЩ, who is, however, important for our welfare.

Although we might have expected the Sun here, because he serves as the ─АdityasтАЩ eye, observing our offenses, we have instead Heaven and Earth, which frame the cosmos. In vs. 6 the nearer gods of the midspace, particularly V─Бta тАШwindтАЩ and the A┼Ыvins, are featured. Rudra appears in both 6 and 7; I donтАЩt quite understand why, but recall first that Agni was identified as Rudra in vs. 1 and may be also in 10d (see also 14b). Moreover, in 6 the punishing aspect of Rudra is emphasized (тАШmansmitingтАЩ, nс╣Ыh├бn-), while in 7 he is paired and/or contrasted with the benevolent P┼лс╣гan under the ambiguous epithet s├║makha-, which means both тАШgood combatantтАЩ and тАШvery generousтАЩ, so his effects on human life are emphasized and he counts as a nearer god, who in fact is the giver of the oblation (havird─Б╠Б-). In the 2nd half of 7 Viс╣гс╣Зu and his three strides return us to the contemplation of the whole cosmos, and vs. 8 functions ring-compositionally with vs. 5: we have the Sun we expected (and didnтАЩt get) in 5, with Aditi standing in for the ─Аdityas in 5, and heaven (though probably the place, not the deity) is the final goal.

Before the Free, before the Swift, defend us: fulfil heaven’s work, all-knowing Jatavedas.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI solicit, Agni, the milk of the cow, essential for the sacrifice; yet immature, (she possesses) the sweet and ripe (fluid); black though she be, yet with her white nutritious milk she maintains mankind in existence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With truth I reverently invoke the (mystical) truth set down [=acquired] from the cow: the raw one [=cow] and the cooked, honeyed (milk) belong together, Agni.
Though she is black, she is swollen with the gleaming gush, with milk for nourishing offspring.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. expresses the beloved paradox about cows and milk, that the cow is тАЬrawтАЭ but her milk тАЬcookedтАЭ (that is, ready to consume), and further that a black cow can still give white milk. These paradoxes describe in the first instance the production of the ritual offering, the milk that will produce the ghee to be poured into the ritual fire. But it may also (esp. the 2nd hemistich) characterize the transition from the night (black cow) to dawn (the gleaming milk) at the dawn sacrifice; see Janert (Dh─Бsi, 29ff.).

The standard interpr. (save for Witzel Got┼Н) take с╣Ыt├йna as the agent with the ppl.

n├нyatam (e.g., Renou тАЬLтАЩOrdre a ├йt├й fix├й par lтАЩOrdre (m├кme)тАЭ). Because the flg. 3 vss.

also begin with с╣Ыt├йna, interpreting the first one outside of the pattern established by the rest seems misguided, esp. given the usual function of initial с╣Ыt├йna (see comm. above on vss. 9-12).

I take the с╣Ыt├бm that I reverently invoke (─лс╕Нe) to represent the paradoxes just discussed – the mystical truth of the cowтАЩs nature – and I interpr. ─Б╠Бg├│с╕е as an ablative phrase, referring to the source of this truth. Most take g├│с╕е as a gen., but this makes ─Б╠Бhard to construe. (The phrase ─Б╠Бg├│с╕е occurs 3x elsewhere, always p─Бda final, twice in this maс╣Зс╕Нala [IV.22.4, 23.6] and once in X [X.100.12]; nowhere is it clear.) At least acdg. to Oldenberg (SBE) and Geldner, the с╣Ыt├бm is actually a reference to the milk. I am skeptical.

On dh─Бs├н- see comm. ad I.62.3, 140.1.

The hapax j─Б╠Бmarya- is opaque; see EWA s.v. My tr. follows JanertтАЩs analysis (Dh─Бsi, 33ff.), that it is a secondary derivative to j─Бm-ara- тАЬdie die Nachkommen N├дhrende.тАЭ GeldnerтАЩs suggestion (n. 9d) that it is related to YAves. z╟Эmar тАШon/in the earthтАЩ (in z╟Эmar-g┼лz-), hence тАШearthlyтАЩ (versus heavenly milk = rain), fits the passage less well.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each of these vss. begins with the resonant and charged instr. с╣Ыt├йna тАШby truthтАЩ, the usual introduction to a truth formulation. Each of the vss. does seem to express a mystical truth about the ritual or its mythic background. There is no obvious connection to the group of vss. that precede (the question vss. of 4cd-8), but if I am correct that we should supply тАШthoughtтАЩ or тАШthoughtsтАЩ in 8cd, where we ask Agni to send them all the way to heaven, it may not be fanciful to think that vss. 9-12 are these very thoughts.

Griffith

I crave the cow’s true gift arranged by Order: though raw, she hath the sweet ripe juice, O Agni.
Though she is black of hue with milk she teemeth, nutritious, brightly shining, all-sustaining.

Oldenberg

I magnify 1 the Rita of the cow 2 ruled by Rita and also by the raw one 3, the honey-sweet, ripe (milk), O Agni. Though being black this (cow) swells of bright drink, of тАж 4 milk.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЛрддреЗрди) рд╕рддреНрдпреЗрди (рдЛрддрдореН) рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН (рдирд┐рдпрддрдореН) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддрдореН (рдИрд│реЗ) рд╕реНрддреМрдореНрдпрдзреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдорд┐ (рдЖ) (рдЧреЛрдГ) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рдЖрдорд╛) рдЕрдкрд░рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╡рдореНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░рд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ (рд╕рдЪрд╛) рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЗрди (рдордзреБрдорддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдордзреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдкрдХреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) (рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛) рд╢реНрдпрд╛рдорд╛ (рд╕рддреА) (рд░реБрд╢рддрд╛) рд╕реБрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреЗрдг (рдзрд╛рд╕рд┐рдирд╛) рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗрди (рдПрд╖рд╛) (рдЬрд╛рдорд░реНрдпреЗрдг) рдЬрд╛рдорд╕реНрдпреЗрджрдВ рдЬрд╛рдордВ рддрджреГрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдпреЗрди рддреЗрди (рдкрдпрд╕рд╛) рджреБрдЧреНрдзреЗрди (рдкреАрдкрд╛рдп) рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрд╕реНрд╡ реерепрее

тАЬThe male Agni, the showerer (of benefits), has been sprinkled by the genitive ine sustaining milk; the giver of food proceeds unswerving (from his course), and the sun, the shedder of rain, has milked the white (fluid) of the udder (of the firmament).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The sun milked: duduhe pс╣Ы┼Ыnir udhas: pr┼Ыni = S┼лrya

Jamison Brereton

Because by truth even the bull, the male Agni, was anointed with the milk on the top [=cream, that is, butter],
not bucking, he went about conferring vigor: the bull as Pr╠е┼Ыni milked gleaming (milk/semen) from his udder.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This 2nd vs. in the truth-formulation sequence both continues the mystical description of the dawn sacrifice and presents another paradox. With regard to the sacrifice, the milk produced in vs. 9 becomes the butter oblation poured on the sacrificial fire, as Geldner discusses. GeldnerтАЩs explanation of the phrase p├бyas─Б pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhy├иna lit.

тАЬthe milk belonging to the backтАЭ is ingenious and (to me) convincing: it is the milk on the top (the image is of a four-legged animal), i.e., the cream, which is made into butter. With the offering of the butter, the fire flames up – allowing it to go about тАЬconferring vigorтАЭ (vayodh─Б╠Б-) in c.

P─Бda c also inaugurates the paradox that is most clearly expressed in d. Agni is characterized as ├бspandam─Бna- in c. As Geldner points out (n. 10c), тИЪspand тАШkick, lunge, jerkтАЩ is only used in Vedic of cows when they are being milked, so Agni is both bull (vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- [a], vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- [d]) and cow. This paradoxical double identity is sharpened in d, where Agni is identified not only as a bull but as Pс╣Ы┼Ыni, the cow who is the mother of the Maruts, and he is the subj. of the quintessential тАЬcowтАЭ verb тИЪduh тАШmilkтАЩ and acts on the quintessential cow body part ┼л╠Бdhar- тАШudderтАЩ. The substance s/he produces from this udder is ┼Ыukr├бm, a word that can refer not only to тАШgleamingтАЩ milk, but is also used to refer to semen. A similar gender-bending milking scenario involving Pс╣Ы┼Ыni and Rudra, the MarutsтАЩ father, is found in II.34.2; see that passage and the comm. thereon. Here Agni may be being identified with Rudra; see the AgniRudra equation in vs. 1 and also the focus on Rudra in the тАЬquestionтАЭ vss. (6d, 7b, 7d). There are a number of passages in the Agni hymns of IV that should be brought into the conversation, though unfortunately what they have to say is obscure: see the тАЬgleaming udderтАЭ (┼Ы├║cy ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е) in IV.1.19 and a neut. entity (quite possibly her udder) belonging to Pс╣Ы┼Ыni in IV.5.7, 10.

What – if anything – this refers to naturalistically is unclear. The tendency among interpr. has been to take it as a reference to rain (see Geldner n. 10d) or to some other celestial phenomenon (L├╝ders 390), but I find BloomfieldтАЩs suggestion (Rig-Veda Repetitions 213) more appropriate to the passage, that the fire, blazing up, тАЬshoots out his flames from his bright udder; he, a bull, is thereby – mirabile dictu – also a pс╣Ы╠е├зni, the heavenly, yielding cow, par excellence.тАЭ Bloomfield also suggests that ┼Ыukr├б- here mean тАШsemenтАЩ, with a zeugma of duduhe: тАЬAs a bull he hath spurted semen, as a Pс╣Ы╠е├зni cow he hath milked his udder.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each of these vss. begins with the resonant and charged instr. с╣Ыt├йna тАШby truthтАЩ, the usual introduction to a truth formulation. Each of the vss. does seem to express a mystical truth about the ritual or its mythic background. There is no obvious connection to the group of vss. that precede (the question vss. of 4cd-8), but if I am correct that we should supply тАШthoughtтАЩ or тАШthoughtsтАЩ in 8cd, where we ask Agni to send them all the way to heaven, it may not be fanciful to think that vss. 9-12 are these very thoughts.

English translation:

тАЬBy the sacrifice, the Aс╣Еgirasas, rending the mountain asunder, have thrown it open, and returned with the cows; the leaders (of holy rites) have arrived happily at the dawn, and the sun was manifest as Agni was engendered.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The sun was manifest: an allusion to the early morning sacrifice with fire, probably instrumental tuted by the Aс╣Еgirasas

Jamison Brereton

By truth they threw open the rock, having split it. The Aс╣Еgirases roared along with the cows.
For blessing the men besieged the dawn; the sun became visible when the fire was born.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The third truth-formulation vs. sets up the Vala myth as the model for the coming of dawn: just as the Aс╣Еgirases breached the Vala cave and let loose the cows, so the human sacrificers break Dawn out of her confinement by kindling the ritual fire. This is the third step in the depiction of the morning ritual. As noted elsewhere (see esp. the published introduction to Maс╣Зс╕Нala IV and to IV.1), the Vala myth and the Aс╣Еgirases play an outsize role in the Agni cycle of IV.

Despite the injunctives of p─Бda a (vy ├аsan) and c (p├бri с╣гadan), I am tempted, with Grassmann, to read anavanta in b, to produce 11 syllables. (Consider the augmented impf. in d, abhavat.) Oldenberg (Noten) considers this restoration possible but not necessary. Hoffmann (Injunk., 209) gives a typical treatment of the vs. in his interpretational system, assuming an injunc. navanta in b.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each of these vss. begins with the resonant and charged instr. с╣Ыt├йna тАШby truthтАЩ, the usual introduction to a truth formulation. Each of the vss. does seem to express a mystical truth about the ritual or its mythic background. There is no obvious connection to the group of vss. that precede (the question vss. of 4cd-8), but if I am correct that we should supply тАШthoughtтАЩ or тАШthoughtsтАЩ in 8cd, where we ask Agni to send them all the way to heaven, it may not be fanciful to think that vss. 9-12 are these very thoughts.

English translation:

тАЬBy sacrifice, Agni, the divine rivers, immortal, unobstructed, continue perpetually to flow with sweet waters, like a horse that is being urged in his speed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

By truth the immortal, unharmable goddesses, the waters with their honeyed floods, o AgniтАФ
like a competitor beating a tattoo at the start(ing posts)тАФshould set to running, to stream forever.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ritual application of this final с╣Ыt├йna vs. is less clear than for the first three. It may simply refer to the waters used at the first soma pressing. Or the ritual aspect may be muted, and the point is to make room for the Vс╣Ыtra myth next to the Vala myth in vs. 11. However, the opt. dadhanyuс╕е seems to reflect a movement from what has happened (the injunctives and preterite indicative of the last few vss.) to what should now happen, which suggests that there should be a ritual application.

The athem. mid. part. -stubh─Бn├б- is isolated, beside the act. them. 1st cl. pres.

st├│bhati, and it is therefore impossible to determine its exact value – including whether it is passive (so, e.g., Oldenberg [SBE], Geldner, Renou) or not. Got┼Н (1st cl., 332 and n.

  1. argues against such a value, on the basis of the intrans. sense of the root, and I have followed him in the non-passive assessment. My tr. тАЬbeat a tattooтАЭ reflects my sense that тИЪstubh is associated esp. with rhythm. As for s├бrga-, lit. тАШsurge, gushтАЩ, it can refer to the instant when the surge is released, hence here the start of a race.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGo not ever, Agni, to the sacrifice of any one who injures us; nor to that of a malevolent neighbour, nor to that of an (unnatural) relation; accept not the due (oblation) from an insincere brother; let us not derive enjoyment from the enemy of a friend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt ever chase after (us, as) the specter of a nobody, a crooked manтАФ neither of a tricky neighbor, nor of a friend. Do not pursue the debt of a dishonest brother (against us), Agni. May we not pay for the тАЬskillтАЭ of a cheating partner.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is very difficult. As I see it, the point of the vs. is to demand that Agni not track down and punish the speaker for the transgressions of others, esp.

others who are close to the speaker and could be mistaken for him. In the first hemistich this notion is expressed by GEN yakс╣г├б- тАЬthe specter/apparition of X,тАЭ where yakс╣г├б- could perhaps best be rendered as Doppelg├дnger.

The first problem one encounters is k├бsya and the puzzle of how an interrogative would interact with the prohibitive m─Б╠Б. The standard solution is to treat k├бsya as an indefinite, without the usual particle (cid, can├б) to mark this value – e.g., Renou тАЬтАж de qui (que ce soit).тАЭ But when the negative n├б is used, the indefinite тАШno one, nothingтАЩ always has the particle. I propose instead to read *ak├бsya тАШof (a) nobodyтАЩ.

With an accent like that of ak├║tra тАШnowhereтАЩ, this interpr. does not require emending the Saс╣Гhit─Б text (which would read m─Б╠Бk├бsya), only the Pp., and the same stem is found three times elsewhere in the same context, at least by my interpr.: V.70.4 m─Б╠Б k├бsya (in a passage very similar to this one), m─Б╠Бk├бsya in VII.94.8, and I.120.8 m─Б╠Б k├бsmai, parallel to m─Б╠Бk├║tr─Б where the Pp. analyzes the first as m─Б╠Бk├бsmai but the 2nd as m─Б╠Бak├║tra. The apparent presence of m─Б╠Б-ak├║tra in this last passage reinforces my interpr. of m─Б╠Бk├бsya / k├бsmai as also containing a privative a-. It might be argued that n├бkis, n├бk─лm (the former of which is very common) and m─Б╠Бkis, m─Б╠Бk─лm lack the indefinitizing particle, but all these forms show univerbation and loss of the accent on the 2nd element.

The form hur├бс╕е has been variously analyzed. Oldenberg (etc) takes it as an adv., and Geldner (etc.) as the gen. of a root noun. (For detailed disc. see Scarlatta [123], who vacillates.) I follow the latter view, but see it not as an abstract but as a personal gen. referring to one of the transgressors. (This seems to be the Witzel Got┼Н interpr., too.) In d Oldenberg suggests emending d├бkс╣гam to yakс╣г├бm (matching the same form in p─Бda a and found elsewhere with bhujema), but it is hard to see how this error could have arisen. I think rather that d├бkс╣гa- is used here ironically or sarcastically.

On m─Б╠Бwith the apparent opt. bhujema, see Hoffmann (Injunk., 95-97), who explains this grammatical anomaly (found several times) as a misinterpr. of expressions with the dat. inf. bhuj├й.

Griffith

Go never to the feast of one who harms us, the treacherous neighbour or. unworthy kinsman.
Punish us not for a false brother’s trespass. Let us riot feel the might of friend or foeman.

Oldenberg

Go never on thy crooked way to the spirit (which avenges the guilt) of anybody 1, of a vassal who has trespassed, or of a friend. Require not (of us),a sinful brother’s debt 2. May we not have to suffer under the spirit which avenges a friend’s or a (hostile) deceiver’s guilt 3.

Geldner

Geh nicht zu der Heimlichkeit irgend eines Unehrlichen, eines t├дuschenden Insassen oder Freundes! Suche nicht die Schuld eines unredlichen Bruders an uns heim, o Agni! Wir m├╢chten nicht den Anschlag eines schelmischen Freundes auskosten!

Grassmann

Verfolg als R├дcher nicht des Menschen Unrecht nicht falscher Freunde oder Hausgenossen, Nicht, Agni, r├дch die Schuld des s├╝nd’gen Bruders, nicht komm uns Noth von feindlichen Genossen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, worthily worshipped, counservator, conciliated (by our offerings), protect us with your protections; enlighten us; entirely extirpate our sin; overcome the great and exulting r─Бkс╣гasas.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Guard us, Agni, with your guards, ever guarding when you are gratified, you good combatant [/very generous].
Spring toward rigid constraint and break it apart; smash demonic force, even though it has grown great.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Once again in this hymn Agni seems to be indirectly identified with Rudra, here by the use of the adj. s├║makha-, used explicitly of Rudra in 7b. The ambiguity of this word works well here also.

Griffith

O Agni, keep us safe with thy protection, loving us, honoured God! and ever guarding.
Beat thou away, destory severe affliction slay e’en the demon when he waxes mighty.

Oldenberg

Protect us, O Agni, with all thy protection, thou who art protected, O martial one 1, and art gladdened (by us). Sparkle forth, and destroy even strong evil! Slay the Rakshas even though it has grown large.

English translation:

тАЬBe propitiated, Agni, by these hymns, accept, hero, these (sacrificial) viands (presented) with praises; be plural ased, Aс╣Еgiras, by our prayers; may the adoration addressed to the gods exalt you. (Taittir─лya Samhit─Б 10.62.5)тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

By reason of these recitations become well disposed, Agni; by reason of our thoughts caress these prizes, o champion.
And enjoy the sacred formulations, Aс╣Еgiras. May the chant favored by the gods bring harmony to you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Vs. 3 also contains forms of both m├бnman- and ┼Ыast├н-.

On s├бm тИЪjс╣Ы see Got┼Н (1st cl., 154-55), who considers the two instances of this lexeme (also in the next hymn, IV.4.8) an individual use of this poet, in the meaning тАШbe welcomeтАЩ [willkommen sein]. In both cases it has a verbal product of the poet as subj. (┼Ыast├н- here, g├нr- IV.4.8). My тАШbring harmonyтАЩ is meant to capture the тАШsingтАЩ feature of the root тИЪjс╣Ы. Perhaps тАШbe harmoniousтАЩ would have been better. For further disc. see ad IV.4.8 below.

English translation:

тАЬAgni, creator, to you who are wise, acquainted with the past, I address, oс╕е sage, these soliciting mysterious words, (these) ever-to-be-recited poems, together with praises and prayers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ever to be recited poems: nivacan─Б(ni) k─Бvy─Бni: nitar─Бm vaktavy─Бni kavibhiс╕е kс╣Ыt─Бni, those which are made by poets ever to be recited

Jamison Brereton

All these devices, the secret words, are for you who know, o ritual adept, AgniтАФ
the enigmas, the poetic compositions are for you, the wise poet. I, the inspired one, have pronounced them in composed thoughts and
solemn speeches.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this vs., see published introduction.

Griffith

To thee who knowest, Agni, thou Disposer, all these wise secret speeches have I uttered,
Sung to thee, Sage, the charming words of wisdom, to thee, O Singer, with. my thoughts and Praises.

Oldenberg

I, the priest, have rehearsed to thee the omniscient one, O Agni, worshipper (of the gods), all these songs, these inmost words, these recitations and words of wisdom, to thee the wise one, with prayers and hymns.

Geldner

Alle diese Weisungen, versteckten Reden habe ich dir, dem Kundigen, o Meister Agni, und die vertraulichen Worte, die Seherworte dir dem Seher in Gedichten und Lobliedern redekundig vorgetragen.

Grassmann

Gesungen hab’ ich alle diese Lieder, o Ordner, Agni, und geheime Worte; dem weisen Seher weisheitsvolle Reden, o Priester, dir mit Spr├╝chen und Gebeten.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрддрд╛) рдПрддрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЗ) (рддреБрднреНрдпрдореН) (рд╡реЗрдзрдГ) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреН (рдиреАрдерд╛рдирд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН (рдирд┐рдгреНрдпрд╛) рдирд┐рд░реНрдгреАрддрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдирд┐рд╡рдЪрдирд╛) рдирд┐рддрд░рд╛рдореБрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗрд╜рд░реНрдерд╛ рдпреИрд╕реНрддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдХрд╡рдпреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп (рдХрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рдХрд╡рд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдЕрд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рд╖рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕реЗрдпрдореН (рдорддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╣ (рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдГ) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА (рдЙрдХреНрдереИрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддреБрдорд░реНрд╣реИрдГ реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╕реИрд╡ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдпрд╛ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпреЗрдд, рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХреИрд░рдзреНрдпреЗрддрд╛рд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ реерезремрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рджрд┐рдХреГрддреНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезремрее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рдХреЗрд▓реЗрд▓реА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдд рдЬрд╛рдгрдгреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЕрд╕рддреЗ. рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рд╡ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдиреА рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрди рд╡ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдШреЗрдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рджреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резрем рее
